Michael brings a deep understanding of our business and a genuine commitment to accelerating our progress,&#8221; said Brian Cornell, chair and chief executive officer of Target Corporation. &#8220;Today, we also reported our second quarter earnings, which showed encouraging signs of recovery, including improved traffic and sales trends &#8212; particularly in our stores &#8212; and disciplined cost management in a challenging retail environment. As we enter the critical back-to-school and holiday seasons, our team remains focused on consistent execution and building momentum as we look ahead to the new year.&#8221;</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:174%">Guidance</font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">For fiscal 2025, the Company is maintaining its expectation of a low-single digit decline in sales, and GAAP EPS of $8.00 to $10.00. Adjusted EPS, which excludes the gains from litigation settlements in the first quarter, is expected to be approximately $7.00 to $9.00. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:174%">Operating Results</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">Net Sales of $25.2 billion in the second quarter were 0.9 percent lower than last year, reflecting a merchandise sales decrease of 1.2 percent, partially offset by a 14.2 percent increase in non-merchandise sales.  Comparable sales decreased 1.9 percent in the second quarter, reflecting a comparable store sales decline of 3.2 percent, partially offset by comparable digital sales growth of 4.3 percent.  Second quarter operating income of $1.3 billion was 19.4 percent lower than last year.</font></div><div style="height:42.75pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">&#8211; more &#8211;</font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div></div></div><div id="i5c428581ba2a431cb01d1957b5044331_7"></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:42.75pt;width:100%"><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">Target Corporation Reports Second Quarter Earnings &#8212; Page 3 of 12</font></div></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">Second quarter operating income margin rate was 5.2 percent in 2025, compared with 6.4 percent in 2024. Second quarter gross margin rate was 29.0 percent, compared with 30.0 percent in 2024, reflecting the net impact of merchandising activities, including higher markdown rates, purchase order cancellation costs, and pressure from category mix, partially offset by lower inventory shrink and growth in advertising and non-merchandise sales. Second quarter SG&#38;A expenses were 0.1 percent lower than in 2024, as increased investments in store remodels and general cost increases across the business were offset by disciplined cost management. Second quarter SG&#38;A expense rate was 21.3 percent, compared with 21.1 percent in 2024, reflecting the deleveraging effect of lower sales. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:174%">Interest Expense and Taxes</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">The Company&#8217;s second quarter 2025 net interest expense was $116 million, compared with $110 million last year, reflecting higher average debt levels in the current year.</font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">Second quarter 2025 effective income tax rate was 23.2 percent, compared with the prior year rate of 22.9 percent, reflecting the impact of higher global minimum taxes. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font><br></font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:174%">Capital Deployment and Return on Invested Capital</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">The Company paid dividends of $509 million in the second quarter, compared with $509 million last year, reflecting a 1.8 percent increase in the dividend per share, offset by the impact of a lower average share count. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">The Company did not repurchase any stock in the second quarter. As of the end of the quarter, the Company had approximately $8.4&#160;billion of remaining capacity under the repurchase program approved by Target&#8217;s Board of Directors in August 2021. </font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">For the trailing twelve months through second quarter 2025, after-tax return on invested capital (ROIC) was 14.3 percent, compared with 16.6 percent for the trailing twelve months through second quarter 2024. The tables in this release provide additional information about the Company&#8217;s ROIC calculation.</font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="height:42.75pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">&#8211; more &#8211;</font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div></div></div><div id="i5c428581ba2a431cb01d1957b5044331_10"></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:42.75pt;width:100%"><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">Target Corporation Reports Second Quarter Earnings &#8212; Page 4 of 12</font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:10pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:174%">Webcast Details</font></div><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:174%">Target will webcast its second quarter earnings conference call at 7&#58;00 a.m. CT today. A replay of the webcast will be provided when available. Since 1946, Target has given 5% of its profit to communities, which today equals millions of dollars a week. In the past, these items have included losses on the early retirement of debt and certain other items that are discretely managed. </font></div><div><font><br></font></div><div style="height:42.75pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div></div><div id="i5c428581ba2a431cb01d1957b5044331_37"></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:42.75pt;width:100%"><div><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:115%">Target Corporation Reports Second Quarter Earnings &#8212; Page 11 of 12</font></div><div><font style="color:#ee2724;font-family:'Calibri',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%">  </font><font style="color:#dbdbdb;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:112%"> </font></div></div><div style="text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Earnings before interest expense and income taxes (EBIT) and earnings before interest expense, income taxes, depreciation and amortization (EBITDA) are non-GAAP financial measures. We believe these measures provide meaningful information about our operational efficiency compared with our competitors by excluding the impact of differences in tax jurisdictions and structures, debt levels, and, for EBITDA, capital investment. These measures are not in accordance with, or an alternative to, GAAP. The most comparable GAAP measure is net earnings. EBIT and EBITDA should not be considered in isolation or as a substitution for analysis of our results as reported in accordance with GAAP. Other companies may calculate EBIT and EBITDA differently, limiting the usefulness of the measures for comparisons with other companies. </font></div><div
